Message-ID: <20010702161104.G6669@hagbard.davep.org>

On Mon, Jul 02, 2001 at 11:45:54AM -0300, Luiz Rafael Culik Guimaraes wrote:

> What i want is to convert one of the harbour html docs(from the
> documentation page) to latex , and then create an new output from hbdoc.
> As I know Latex is an important Kind of Document to linux, As i heard you
> can create an variety of document for linux with source being an latex
> file.

LaTeX isn't as generally common in the GNU/Linux world as you might think. I
can't think of a reason why it would be important to a GNU/Linux user to
have the harbour documentation as LaTeX source. Sure, it might be handy but
I can't think of a reason why it would be important.

I'd have thought that sgml-tools (AKA LinuxDOC SGML) would be of more use in
this regard (see the source for the harbour FAQ as an example). One of the
targets for that is LaTeX. It targets many document types:

,----
| davep@hagbard:~$ rpm-describe sgml-tools
| SGMLtools is a text formatting package based on SGML (Standard
| Generalized Markup Language).  SGMLtools allows you to produce LaTeX,
| HTML, GNU info, LyX, RTF, plain text (via groff), and other format
| outputs from a single SGML source.  SGMLtools is intended for writing
| technical software documentation.
`----

> Btw, ill send the html that i want to convert to you tonight

You might also want to give me a pointer to the conversion tool you had in
mind.

--

<URL:http://freshmeat.net/projects/sgmltools/> but neither of the links

while I was searching. I can't vouch for it as I've never seen it before but

that it is based around python <URL:http://www.python.org/> and I know from
experience that python runs fine under Windows.

Hi,

*Question:
 How can I add a codeblock or a function call to URLDownloadToFile()

A little explanation:
---------------------
There is a API function URLDownloadToFile() in URLMON.DLL.
This is what I have so far, and it works ok!
,---------------
|DLL32 Function URLDownloadToFile (;
|               pCaller    AS DWORD ,;
|               szURL      AS LPSTR ,;
|               szFileName AS LPSTR ,;
|               dwResetved AS DWORD ,;
|               lpfnCB     AS DWORD) ;
|      AS LONG PASCAL FROM "URLDownloadToFileA" LIB "URLMON.dll"
`---------------------------------

But I also want a progress bar. The last parameter to URL..() is:
"Address of the caller's IBindStatusCallback interface."

How can I pass a Progress function as "IBindStatusCallback"??

Please see
http://msdn.microsoft.com/library/default.asp?url=/workshop/networking/m
oniker/reference/functions/URLDownloadToFile.asp
for more info.

Thanks!

Regards,

Indeed. The fascinating thing, though (you can try this if you like) is if
you start a 32x32 24-bit bitmap in paintbrush, and copy it to the
clipboard, you can paste it into imagedit with no loss of colour depth.
Even when you save it (from imagedit) it doesn't appear to change. It's
only when you try looking at it from somewhere else that it becomes
apparent that imagedit has screwed you. :-)

> Anyone got a decent icon editor? :-)

The one that I have is from PC Magazine, but they don't seem to offer
it anymore. It's fairly decent, but only supports up to 256 color icons.
I'm no artist, so I took the Harbour logo JPG and reduced it to a 32x19
image in a 32x32 icon using PMView 2000 (http://www.pmview.com/). I've
attached three versions of it: A 24-bit icon, a 256 adaptive color icon,
and a 256 system color icon.

From harbourtalk@matrixlist.com  Sun Jul 15 09:56:22 2001
From: harbourtalk@matrixlist.com (Dave Pearson)
Date: Sun, 15 Jul 2001 09:56:22 +0100
Subject: [HarbourTalk] Help with MS Visual C++
In-Reply-To: <003c01c10c46$0aa00db0$6400a8c0@patrick2>; from harbour@winfakt.com on Sat, Jul 14, 2001 at 11:19:10AM +0200
References: <002c01c10c3f$8516ee30$6400a8c0@patrick2> <003c01c10c46$0aa00db0$6400a8c0@patrick2>
Message-ID: <20010715095622.G25750@hagbard.davep.org>

On Sat, Jul 14, 2001 at 11:19:10AM +0200, Patrick Mast, Harbour wrote:

> I'm starting to write a MS Visual C++ app. I have some questions:
> 
> - How can I write a sMsg to a log file?

How you do this shouldn't be any different from how you'd normally write
something to a file in a C++ application. For example (my C++ is a little
rusty so please excuse any mistakes):

-- cut here ----------------------------------------------------------------
#include <fstream>
#include <string>

void log_message( char *file, char *msg )
{
    ofstream log;

    log.open( file );

    if ( log.good() )
    {
        log << msg << endl;
        log.close();
    }
}

int main( void )
{
    log_message( "log.txt", "Hello, World!" );
    
    return( 0 );
}
-- cut here ----------------------------------------------------------------

Obviously, if you're going to be doing lots of logging, you probably don't
want to be opening and closing the file for each logged item. Modify to
taste.

> - How can I delete a file?

Doubtless there's some MSVC++ specific method of doing this in their
framework but, unless I'm mistaken, good old unlink() still exists in C++.

From harbourtalk@matrixlist.com  Sun Jul 15 09:47:46 2001
From: harbourtalk@matrixlist.com (Dave Pearson)
Date: Sun, 15 Jul 2001 09:47:46 +0100
Subject: [HarbourTalk] Help with MS Visual C++
In-Reply-To: <002c01c10c3f$8516ee30$6400a8c0@patrick2>; from harbour@winfakt.com on Sat, Jul 14, 2001 at 10:32:29AM +0200
References: <3822442500.20010713162442@abacuslaw.com> <002c01c10c3f$8516ee30$6400a8c0@patrick2>
Message-ID: <20010715094746.F25750@hagbard.davep.org>

On Sat, Jul 14, 2001 at 10:32:29AM +0200, Patrick Mast, Harbour wrote:

> Just learned that __argv[x] holds the parameters. Thanks! ;-)
> 
> How can I do this in C:

The subject suggests you're trying to learn C++, don't forget that it's
quite different from C. Also, I'd have thought that if you're doing this
using MS's Windows framework library (MCL isn't it?) that it would provide
useful levels of abstraction for getting at this sort of stuff. It's
probably worth searching the help on the framework for this.

> if !Empty( __argc[1] )
> {
>   ...
> }

Don't you mean __argv[1]? __argc is usually a count of the parameters
passed. Moreover, you don't want to be doing what you're trying to do here.
First you want to be checking if the array is that big. The size of the
array is dictated by the number of parameters passed to the application. So,
you probably want something akin to:

,----
| if ( __argc > 1 )  /* 1 == no parameters because of argv[ 0 ] */
| {
|     ...
| }
`----

Now, if you really do want to check that a given argument isn't empty you'd
probably do something like:

-- cut here ----------------------------------------------------------------
#include <stdio.h>

int main( int argc, char **argv )
{
    if ( argc > 1 )
    {
        if ( strlen( argv[ 1 ] ) )
        {
            printf( "You passed \"%s\"\n", argv[ 1 ] );
        }
        else
        {
            printf( "You passed an empty argument\n" );
        }
    }
    else
    {
        printf( "Not talking to me?\n" );
    }
    
    return( 0 );
}
-- cut here ----------------------------------------------------------------

The above handles no arguments:

,----
| davep@hagbard:~/temp$ ./foo
| Not talking to me?
`----

an argument:

,----
| davep@hagbard:~/temp$ ./foo hello
| You passed "hello"
`----

and an empty argument:

,----
| davep@hagbard:~/temp$ ./foo ""
| You passed an empty argument
`----

As is usual with C/C++, strlen() isn't the only method of doing this sort of
thing. I could just as easily have written:

-- cut here ----------------------------------------------------------------
#include <stdio.h>

int main( int argc, char **argv )
{
    if ( argc > 1 )
    {
        if ( *argv[ 1 ] )
        {
            printf( "You passed \"%s\"\n", argv[ 1 ] );
        }
        else
        {
            printf( "You passed an empty argument\n" );
        }
    }
    else
    {
        printf( "Not talking to me?\n" );
    }
    
    return( 0 );
}
-- cut here ----------------------------------------------------------------

(note *argv[ 1 ] instead of strlen()).

On Sun, Jul 15, 2001 at 09:56:22AM +0100, Dave Pearson wrote:

> How you do this shouldn't be any different from how you'd normally write
> something to a file in a C++ application. For example (my C++ is a little
> rusty so please excuse any mistakes):
> 
> -- cut here ----------------------------------------------------------------
> [SNIP]
> -- cut here ----------------------------------------------------------------

And there was a mistake. The file was being opened in overwrite mode each
time when we wanted append mode.

This:

-- cut here ----------------------------------------------------------------
#include <fstream>
#include <string>

void log_message( string file, string msg )
{
    ofstream log;

    log.open( file.c_str(), ios::app );

    if ( log.good() )
    {
        log << msg << endl;
        log.close();
    }
}

int main( void )
{
    log_message( "log.txt", "Hello, World!" );
    
    return( 0 );
}
-- cut here ----------------------------------------------------------------

Works as intended (and uses C++ strings too, which seems to make more
sense).

[]

Question for the C++ types out there. With my C++ compiler:

,----
| davep@hagbard:~$ c++ --version
| egcs-2.91.66
`----

ofstream::open() won't accept a `string' as the filename parameter (hence
"file.c_str()" in the above code, it expects a `const char *'. I'm surprised
to find that there isn't an overloaded version of ofstream::open() that
takes a `string'. Is this an omission in C++ itself or is it simply the
version of GCC that I've got here?

Subject: [HarbourTalk] Ready to learn SQL
In-Reply-To: <009d01c11129$6dd19e70$6400a8c0@patrick2>; from harbour@winfakt.com on Fri, Jul 20, 2001 at 04:36:57PM +0200
References: <009d01c11129$6dd19e70$6400a8c0@patrick2> <009e01c1112c$8672fac0$6400a8c0@patrick2> <001401c10e90$13c93f00$6400a8c0@patrick2> <009d01c11129$6dd19e70$6400a8c0@patrick2>

On Fri, Jul 20, 2001 at 04:36:57PM +0200, Patrick Mast, Harbour wrote:
> Hi,
> 
> I'm ready to learn SQL.
> Is it a replacement for DBF?

No, it's a language, DBF is a file format. Different things. You can, for
example, use SQL to interact with DBF files.

> Can it doe everything DBF can do?

See above.

> WHY should we use SQL? (mySQL)

There is no "should". You'd use it if it makes sense for you to use it. If
it doesn't, don't use it.

On Fri, Jul 20, 2001 at 04:59:07PM +0200, Patrick Mast, Harbour wrote:

> Is a SQL dtabase file a collection of many database files?

See above, SQL is a language, it has nothing to do with files.

,----[ From The Free On-line Dictionary of Computing (13 Mar 01) ]
| SQL
| 
|    <language, database, standard> /S Q L/ An industry-standard
|    language for creating, updating and, querying relational
|    database management systems.
| 
|    SQL was developed by IBM in the 1970s for use in System R.
|    It is the de facto standard as well as being an ISO and
|    ANSI standard.  It is often embedded in general purpose
|    programming languages.
| 
|    The first SQL standard, in 1986, provided basic language
|    constructs for defining and manipulating tables of data; a
|    revision in 1989 added language extensions for referential
|    integrity and generalised integrity constraints.  Another
|    revision in 1992 provided facilities for schema manipulation
|    and data administration, as well as substantial enhancements
|    for data definition and data manipulation.
| 
|    Development is currently underway to enhance SQL into a
|    computationally complete language for the definition and
|    management of persistent, complex objects.  This includes:
|    generalisation and specialisation hierarchies, multiple
|    inheritance, user defined data types, triggers and
|    assertions, support for knowledge based systems,
|    recursive query expressions, and additional data
|    administration tools.  It also includes the specification of
|    abstract data types (ADTs), object identifiers, methods,
|    inheritance, polymorphism, encapsulation, and all of the
|    other facilities normally associated with object data
|    management.
| 
|    The emerging SQL3 standard is expected to be complete in
|    1998.
| 
|    According to Allen G. Taylor, SQL does _not_ stand for
|    "Structured Query Language".  That, like "SEQUEL" (and its
|    pronunciation /see'kw*l/), was just another unofficial name
|    for a precursor of SQL.  However, the IBM SQL Reference manual
|    for DB2 and Craig Mullins's "DB2 Developer's Guide" say SQL
|    _does_ stand for "Structured Query Language".
| 
|    SQL Standards (http://www.jcc.com/sql_stnd.html).
| 
|    An SQL parser
|    (ftp://ftp.uu.net/published/oreilly/nutshell/lexyacc/) is
|    described in "Lex & Yacc", by Levine, Mason & Brown published
|    by O'Reilly.
| 
|    The 1995 SQL Reunion: People, Projects, and Politics
|    (http://www.mcjones.org/System_R/SQL_Reunion_95/).
| 
|    ["A Guide to the SQL Standard", C.J. Date, A-W 1987].
| 
|    ["SQL for Dummies", Allen G. Taylor, IDG Books Worldwide].
| 
|    (2000-07-07)
`----

From harbourtalk@matrixlist.com  Fri Jul 20 19:11:46 2001
From: harbourtalk@matrixlist.com (Alexander S.Kresin)
Date: Fri, 20 Jul 2001 22:11:46 +0400
Subject: [HarbourTalk] Re: Ready to learn SQL
In-Reply-To: <00aa01c1113b$ab29a3a0$6400a8c0@patrick2>
References: <00aa01c1113b$ab29a3a0$6400a8c0@patrick2>
Message-ID: <5518702062.20010720221146@belacy.belgorod.su>

Patrick,

PMH> So, what's the benefit on using SQL?
PMH> Who uses SQL and why?

 Usually, when people talk about SQL, they mean two things:
 SQL as language and SQL DBMS.

 1. SQL is a language, a method of access to the databases, independent
 of their physical format. Some simplest examples, just to be more
 clear, what is it:

  CREATE TABLE customers
     ( cust_id numeric(6,0), cust_name char(20) )

  INSERT INTO customers
     VALUES ( 124, 'Abcd corporation' )

  UPDATE customers SET cust_name = 'Abcd Inc.' WHERE cust_id = 124

  SELECT cust_name FROM customers WHERE cust_id = 124

 2. SQL DBMS - this is a lot of DBMS's ( Oracle, MS SQL, Informix,
 DB2, postgreSQL, mySQL, ... ), which uses SQL as the main tool for
 the access to the data.
 There are tables - the flat data set ( as dbf ) and databases - sets
 of tables.
 The benefit of using SQL DBMS, as I understand it, is the following:
 You can create database as a mirror of your information system,
 create all tables in it, describe relations between tables and DBMS
 itself will keep your data in valid state. There are such things , as
 triggers, where you can describe the operations, which DBMS will
 execute while appending a record, deleting, etc. There may be
 replication support - copying data between servers, so all related
 servers will have the same state of data. Stored procedures, which
 executes on server and other features.
 And all these will be handled by DBMS itself, independent of user's
 applications. This increases the safety, stability of databases ( if
 there is clever db admin, of course :) ).


Best regards,
 Alexander
http://members.xoom.com/alkresin/



From harbourtalk@matrixlist.com  Fri Jul 20 19:59:10 2001
From: harbourtalk@matrixlist.com (Antonio Linares)
Date: Fri, 20 Jul 2001 20:59:10 +0200
Subject: [HarbourTalk] Ready to learn SQL
In-Reply-To: <00aa01c1113b$ab29a3a0$6400a8c0@patrick2>
Message-ID: <000201c1114e$0f80b8e0$0f2aa8c0@first>

Patrick,

> Who uses SQL and why?

Normally very large companies as banks, insurance companies, etc...

Why they use it ?

Most of the times it is because they have so many different
applications running, developed by so many different software 
development companies, even on so many different operating systems, 
that finally they do need to separate their databases from their apps.

What is the advantadge of using SQL ?

They may directly query or/and perform certain tasks on their 
databases, without requiring an application to do that task. 
Think of it like a DBU: You open the database and you do what 
you need with the data on your tables. No need for an app.

Besides that, those large companies get the freedom to use
any development language, as far as those languages *talk* SQL.


Antonio

SQL is a "language", if you like, for using databases. Any database - even 
DBFs. You can ask for data, add/modify/delete data, and even define 
tables/indexes etc with it.

> Can it doe everything DBF can do?

Hopefully from my above explanation you see that this question doesn't 
really make sense.
 
> WHY should we use SQL? (mySQL)

There are databases which can *only* be accessed using SQL. Informix and 
Oracle are like this. Once we have an SQL layer in Clipper, we can very 
easily move a DBF application to one of these "big iron" databases.

From harbourtalk@matrixlist.com  Sat Jul 21 07:27:19 2001
From: harbourtalk@matrixlist.com (Dave Pearson)
Date: Sat, 21 Jul 2001 07:27:19 +0100
Subject: [HarbourTalk] Ready to learn SQL
In-Reply-To: <00aa01c1113b$ab29a3a0$6400a8c0@patrick2>; from harbour@winfakt.com on Fri, Jul 20, 2001 at 06:47:31PM +0200
References: <20010720170701.I3686@hagbard.davep.org> <00aa01c1113b$ab29a3a0$6400a8c0@patrick2>
Message-ID: <20010721072719.M3686@hagbard.davep.org>

On Fri, Jul 20, 2001 at 06:47:31PM +0200, Patrick Mast, Harbour wrote:

> So, what's the benefit on using SQL?

They're many and varied. It has it's downsides (as a language it sucks in
huge amounts IMO) in some situations but it has it's upsides in others. I
see others have posted reasons so I won't covers theirs. From my point of
view it's useful because it's (more or less) a standard language that can be
used all over the place, I use it in python, perl, C, emacs, Delphi, etc.
Being able to (more or less) write portable queries is a very handy thing.

The fact that you generally build your queries up as strings is handy too. A
common question for people who've only ever used an Xbase language and are
trying to expand out into other languages is "where's the macro compiler?".
Most often the macro compile is used when building dynamic query systems
(codeblocks taking care of most other instances of macro usage). When you've
got SQL around a lack of a macro compiler isn't a problem any more. Building
a database query is as simple as concatenating a string.

The major problem I have with SQL is that, to get the best out of it, you're
really got to get into it. In my experience (I'm starting to re-learn it now
as we just recently lost out SQL expert) you can't do non-trivial stuff
without knowing it really well. Not that I have a problem with ensuring that
people learn things properly, far from it, but it does mean that such a
"small" language has a tricky learning curve.

> Who uses SQL and why?

That's a pretty big question that cant' really be answered in any useful
sense.

> in SQL languages or are they database engines?

As far as I know there is a definitive ANSI SQL standard, but (like so 
many languages) vendors tend to add their own little extensions. Informix 
has quite a few, like "alter fragment" to "defragment" a table on disk.

> Is mySQL a database engine?

AFAIK, yes.

> Can I use a Harbour/Clipper app WITHOUT RDD and use mySQL?

Hmm. Well, if mySQL has a C library to access it, and you write the 
wrapper functions yourself, then I don't see why not.

Patrick,

PMH> How does mySQL fit in this picture?

 mySQL is one of SQL DBMS's . It has its own database format, API,
 etc. Its advantages are more simplicity in comparison with other SQL
 DBMS's, higher speed. Its disadvantages are, as usually, related with
 its advantages - it doesn't support some features, usual in SQL
 world: transactions, triggers and some others.
 
PMH> If SQL is a language, why are there so many SQL flavors? Is It a flavor
PMH> in SQL languages or are they database engines?

 There is a standard for SQL language, but, as usually, real
 implementations has some limitations/additions.

PMH> Is mySQL a database engine?

 Yes.
 
PMH> Can I use a Harbour/Clipper app WITHOUT RDD and use mySQL?

 Clipper - don't sure, Harbour - yes.

 John,

JS> Is there an SQL server for DOS that I can use to access  .DBFs on my server.

 Don't sure that I understand clear, what you mean. Is your server
 works under MS-DOS ?

JS> I understand that another benefit of SQL vs. an xBASE product, is when you 
JS> do a search (say using LOCATE), all of the records are transferred across 
JS> the lan to your node, where they are searched on your computer vs. an SQL 
JS> server, where only the 'found' records are sent down the lan, thereby 
JS> reducing transmission time on a serial link.

 Don't confuse client-server with SQL. The above is correct for any
 client-server solution, not obligatory SQL. For example, ADS is
 client-server xBase solution, but isn't SQL DBMS ( only since 6.0
 version they includes some SQL DBMS features, but I don't think that
 it can be called SQL DBMS even now ). There are some other
 client-server xBase systems, too, which aren't SQL DBMS. But for all
 them the above is right.

From harbourtalk@matrixlist.com  Wed Jul 25 00:44:07 2001
From: harbourtalk@matrixlist.com (Lorenzo Fiorini)
Date: Wed, 25 Jul 2001 01:44:07 +0200
Subject: [HarbourTalk] Re: mySQL
Message-ID: <000901c1149a$8fbafd00$df21623e@teamwork.lan>

Patrick,

I've already investigated the possibility to move my FiveWin Clipper 5.3b
DBFCDX apps to Harbour/mySQL. I've made some considerations and I hope they
can help you: ( DISCLAIMER: these are only my personal opinions, please
don't ask me any evidence of this )

- moving from DBFs to an SQL remote engine will be necessary
- the key words for me are "remote", "security", "replication" ( SQL is
simply the most used standard for accessing remote DBMS )
- remote means that you need only an ip address, a port, a user id and a
password to access your data. This means also no more optimistic locking
problems and server OS indipendence
- security means that you can decide that a user ( or a program ) can only
"read" but never "write" or "zap" that table
- replication means you can have a copy of your data to expose to the public
while keeping the master database secure
- Harbour has a directory contrib/mysql that works very well thanks to
Maurilio and Alexander ( among the others that made Harbour a reality )
- mySQL is free works well in Windows and Linux and runs on a Pentium 100
40MB RAM PC ( I have one ) and it has an utility called dbf2mysql so you can
move your DBFs easily ( it is not the only possibility )

Unfortunatly it means also:

- rethink the logic of many parts of the program
- no more SEEK
- locking a record can be difficult to impossible ( depends on the DBMS you
choose )
- change the USE TABLE ( operation that does nothing but setting a buffer )
to SELECT ....... FROM TABLE ( operation that can takes milliseconds,
seconds, minutes or hours for large tables with a lot of fields not indexed
correctly with multiple joins )
- no more SEEK
- moving from RDD syntax to an object data syntax ( TABLE->FIELD becomes
oQuery:FieldName etc. )
- a lot of other problems....................... and last but not least NO
MORE SEEK

I'm very interested in opinions and experiences of the community members
about the move to SQL.

Best regards.
Lorenzo







From harbourtalk@matrixlist.com  Wed Jul 25 00:52:58 2001
From: harbourtalk@matrixlist.com (harbourtalk@matrixlist.com)
Date: Wed, 25 Jul 2001 09:52:58 +1000
Subject: [HarbourTalk] Re: mySQL
Message-ID: <OFBB2FDB92.F8342DB1-ONCA256A93.0082FA45@cor.bmi.bunge.com.au>

Was it Eddie that first came up with the idea of "plugging" SQL into the
RDD system, with commands like this:

use (select * from mytable) alias fred

So that "fred" could now be used as if it was a dbf? That'd be a great
idea. I don't know what the best way to implement it would be. If the
programmer knew that any queries used as aliases were cached in memory,
they would probably only use sensible queries. Otherwise there may be a way
to cache queries on disk as dbfs or some other file.

This would address many of the "problems" outlined below.

Mabster

> while keeping the master database secure
> - Harbour has a directory contrib/mysql that works very well thanks to
> Maurilio and Alexander ( among the others that made Harbour a reality )
> - mySQL is free works well in Windows and Linux and runs on a Pentium 100
> 40MB RAM PC ( I have one ) and it has an utility called dbf2mysql so you
can
> move your DBFs easily ( it is not the only possibility )
>
> Unfortunatly it means also:
>
> - rethink the logic of many parts of the program
> - no more SEEK
> - locking a record can be difficult to impossible ( depends on the DBMS
you
> choose )
> - change the USE TABLE ( operation that does nothing but setting a
buffer )
> to SELECT ....... FROM TABLE ( operation that can takes milliseconds,
> seconds, minutes or hours for large tables with a lot of fields not
indexed
> correctly with multiple joins )
> - no more SEEK
> - moving from RDD syntax to an object data syntax ( TABLE->FIELD becomes
> oQuery:FieldName etc. )
> - a lot of other problems....................... and last but not least NO
> MORE SEEK
>
> I'm very interested in opinions and experiences of the community members
> about the move to SQL.
>
> Best regards.
> Lorenzo
>
>
>
>
>
>
> _______________________________________________
> HarbourTalk mailing list
> HarbourTalk@matrixlist.com
> http://www.matrixlist.com/mailman/listinfo/harbourtalk

From harbourtalk@matrixlist.com  Wed Jul 25 10:25:49 2001
From: harbourtalk@matrixlist.com (harbourtalk@matrixlist.com)
Date: Wed, 25 Jul 2001 19:25:49 +1000
Subject: [HarbourTalk] Re: mySQL
Message-ID: <OF190AE71D.93A211D9-ONCA256A94.0033AAB4@dingoblue.net.au>

It wouldn't. What you'd need to look at, though, is exactly what to 
replace the "use blah alias blah" lines with. For example, you wouldn't 
just use (select * from table) at the top of the file. You'd have to use 
exactly as much data as you need *each* time you need to access it (so as 
to conserve network/database access).

The solution has to do with preparing cursors etc, but I haven't done 
enough true client/server to comment properly (I've been spoiled by 
Delphi).

From harbourtalk@matrixlist.com  Wed Jul 25 11:24:05 2001
From: harbourtalk@matrixlist.com (Schalk van Zyl)
Date: Wed, 25 Jul 2001 12:24:05 +0200
Subject: [HarbourTalk] Re: mySQL
Message-ID: <01c114f3$ee683620$3ec809c0@IS2.intranet>

A powerfull feature of SQL-languages which we lack is 'select-lists'.
An instruction like SELECT CUSTOMER-FILE WITH TOWN="ABCD"
creates a 'select-list' of (indexed) record-id's and subsequent reads will
bring up records from the select-list (skip).

Schalk

From harbourtalk@matrixlist.com  Wed Jul 25 17:39:13 2001
From: harbourtalk@matrixlist.com (Lorenzo Fiorini)
Date: Wed, 25 Jul 2001 18:39:13 +0200
Subject: [HarbourTalk] Re: mySQL
Message-ID: <001201c11528$5a0819c0$0701a8c0@teamwork.lan>

Don Lowenstein wrote......

DL> Do you think it will convert "seamlessly"?

DL> Regarding your thoughts below, the "SEEK" command doesn't appear to be
DL> the
DL> problem to me.  Simply select from this table for this key (use of the
seek
DL> command presumes an active index).

DL> My question is, if I SEEK, can I then "move the record pointer by 1" to
DL> simulate the "SKIP" command?

Analyzing my code I found many situations where it is necessary a major
rethink
For examples the first SEEK of a report is not a problem since usually you
go from a key to another using an index so it could be easily translated in
"SELECT .... WHERE KEY BETWEEN " + cFirst + " AND " + cLast. The problem are
the SEEKs that you use to decode the fields that are in the main tables with
descriptions that you have in the related tables. Every select means sending
it to the server, the server will parse it, it will run the optimizer to
understand if it can use some indexes or it has to do a linear search and if
it has to create a temporary table or the datas can be managed in ram and so
on. Surely you can't convert every seek into a select.

Updates and Inserts are other problems. In xBASE is easy to mix retrieving
and updating or inserting, in SQL you have different statements so you have
to SELECT or UPDATE or INSERT one at time.

This does not change my opinion that moving from DBFs to a SQL DBMS is a
must. What I'm wondering is which is the best path to move actual Clipper
code. Like many of us I'm using Clipper since 1986 and my code has 15 years
of debugging and development ( some functions are still from DBIII days ).

I think that would be a good idea to define and implement a "standard"
Harbour Data Object interface to map in the ODBC contrib, mySQL contrib and
all the other interfaces that will come ( I remember someone who wanted to
create an interface to Interbase ). If not it is very likely that every
programmer will use different classes and interfaces so if you want to move
from mySQL to MSSQL because your customer is a M$ shop you will have to
rewrite everything.

M$ Foxpro ODBC driver works well with 5.3b DBF/CDX so it could be the way to
start the convertion and still working on DBFs. I think a good ODBC support
is a "minimal" requirement for a 32 bit Windows language ( there is also a
UNIXODBC ). Harbour + ODBC has helped me to import ACCESS databases in my
DBFs and to move data from my DBFs to my Apache, PHP , mySQL applications.

Any opinion or idea ?

Best regards.
Lorenzo.

Subject: [HarbourTalk] Help with C and Alloc
In-Reply-To: <001301c11534$00d498e0$79d4d7c8@culik>
References: <001301c11534$00d498e0$79d4d7c8@culik>
Message-ID: <200107251420.000000T0@Internet>

** Reply to message from "Luiz Rafael Culik Guimaraes"
<culik@nh.conex.com.br> on Wed, 25 Jul 2001 15:00:58 -0300

> I need to return the szBuff variable. My question is, If I call the free
> before the return, i?ll lost the content of szBuff.

You'll be returning a pointer to a freed memory block. The results will
vary by platform. On some platforms, you'll still be able to access the
compressed string, but only until another memory allocation takes place.
On other platforms, attempting to access a freed memory block will
result in some type of out-of-bounds memory access exception. And on yet
other platforms, you'll end up accessing a block of memory that has been
zeroed. And and still other platforms, the results will vary, seemingly
randomly.

You either have to make the caller free the string, which is what many
Harbbour C routines do, or you have to have the caller pass an
appropriately sized buffer as a second argument to the function.
-- 
David G. Holm, Set Captain and all around
Harbour Project Clipper Compatibility fanatic.

From harbourtalk@matrixlist.com  Thu Jul 26 17:39:49 2001
From: harbourtalk@matrixlist.com (Ron Pinkas)
Date: Thu, 26 Jul 2001 09:39:49 -0700
Subject: [HarbourTalk] Help with C and Alloc
In-Reply-To: <009501c115d0$e09dbfa0$cdd4d7c8@culik>
Message-ID: <LOBBKAFMMFGJIKLMEPAKMENBDOAA.Ron@Profit-Master.com>

Luiz,

> > Agree. Or, you could copy the result into the allocated space pointed to
> by
> > the passed parameter, so the input parameter becomes an In/Out
> parameter.
>
> Can you Post the Code that i´ve post on the previews email. you use your
> suggestion.
> I´m afraid that i could not fully understand your suggestion

//--------------------------------------------------//
void pascal ZEXPORT COMPRESSSTRING( /*char *szString*/ )
{
  char *szString = _parc(1); // Using Clipper parameter.
  ULONG ulLen = strlen( szString );
  ULONG ulBuffLen;
  char *szBuff;

  szBuff = ( char * )malloc( ulLen+1 );
  ulBuffLen = ulLen + 1;

  compress( szBuff, &ulBuffLen,  szString, ulLen);

  //strncpy( szString, szBuff, ulBuffLen ); // If using c parameter
  _storclen( szBuff, ulBuffLen, 1 ); // Using Clipper parameter BY
REFERENCE.
  _retclen( szBuff, ulBuffLen ); // And/or returning the value.
  free(szBuff);
}
//--------------------------------------------------//

In Clipper:

sString := "Some string here"
CompressString( @sString ) // Note pass by reference.

In C:

Just comment the Clipper lines, and uncomment the C parameter.

Ron

From harbourtalk@matrixlist.com  Thu Jul 26 21:28:13 2001
From: harbourtalk@matrixlist.com (Ron Pinkas)
Date: Thu, 26 Jul 2001 13:28:13 -0700
Subject: [HarbourTalk] Help with C and Alloc
In-Reply-To: <001501c11608$b1894f80$25d4d7c8@culik>
Message-ID: <LOBBKAFMMFGJIKLMEPAKKENHDOAA.Ron@Profit-Master.com>

Luiz,

> > > Can you Post the Code that i´ve post on the previews email.
> you use your
> > > suggestion.
> > > I´m afraid that i could not fully understand your suggestion
> >
>
> Thanks for the help.
> With the Harbour API i already  got this function working.
> But as C  API i wasn´t having luck

The following should work:

//--------------------------------------------------//
void pascal ZEXPORT COMPRESSSTRING( char *szString )
{
   ULONG ulLen = strlen( szString );
   ULONG ulBuffLen;
   char *szBuff;

   szBuff = ( char * )malloc( ulLen+1 );
   ulBuffLen = ulLen + 1;

   compress( szBuff, &ulBuffLen,  szString, ulLen);

   strncpy( szString, szBuff, ulBuffLen ); // Now the pointer of the
original string will point to the compressed string.
   free(szBuff);
}

Please note that the compress() function you call, is using the principal of
passing a pointer for the return value, just like David pointed out.

In my version above the caller will call COMPRESSSTRING( szString ) and
after the call szString will have the value of the compressed string.

Ron

From harbourtalk@matrixlist.com  Mon Jul 30 16:06:27 2001
From: harbourtalk@matrixlist.com (Antonio Linares)
Date: Mon, 30 Jul 2001 17:06:27 +0200
Subject: [HarbourTalk] Replacements for unsuported Win16 functions
In-Reply-To: <000101c117ae$3812f780$0f2aa8c0@first>
Message-ID: <000f01c11909$350366e0$0f2aa8c0@first>

I have been all day long trying to port
Windows placeable metafiles (Aldus format)
from 16 bits to 32 bits routines.

I finally got it working :-)

But it is unbeliebable how many functions
M$ hasn't ported from 16 to 32 bits. Here
there is one more. I may finally write a
book "Replacements for unsuported Win16 functions
under Win32 API" :-)

#ifdef __FLAT__

HGLOBAL SetMetaFileBits( HMETAFILE hmf )
{
   CONST BYTE * pData = GlobalLock( ( HGLOBAL ) hmf );
   HMETAFILE hmf32  = SetMetaFileBitsEx( GlobalSize( ( HGLOBAL ) hmf ),
pData );

   GlobalUnlock( ( HGLOBAL) hmf );
   return ( HGLOBAL ) hmf32;
}

#endif

This is not directly related to Harbour... but hopefully
Harbour APIs, as it eveolves, may never become so unconsistent
as these M$ ones,


Antonio
